< Review>
I usually look at their specials menu though. Whenever there's something called "Short on Cash" I always get it. They give you a 1lb whole lobster, homemade chips, coleslaw, and bread n butter. For around $20, it's the best deal on lobster in the store in my opinion.People often rave about the blueberry lemonade. It's quite tasty, but I don't find myself always getting it. Besides the Short on Cash special, the lobster chowder is quite delicious. As for their lobster rolls, the highlight is their bread they use. I love the grilled buns that taste of delicious butter. Also, if you get a chance to have some of their baguette rolls, it's absolutely amazing.</Review>

<user>103942471738003126654< /user>< name>
Aaron Sluis< /name>
< date>
1580765006062< /date>
<rate>3</rate>< Review>
I'm torn on this review.

On one hand, it's terrific that a business like this can exist at all.  If you are a hobbyist or like to repair things, this is (potentially) a great resource.  The people running it do seem to care, even if they're not always the most personable.  I see some complaints about them being rude, but I don't buy it.

As a brick&mortar business, however, it lets me down.  I've gone in for basic parts several times - lamp-cord switch, XT power connectors, etc. - and they're out of stock.  Looking around, empty shelves/bins are not uncommon.  It seems they have difficulty keeping stocked up.

Prices are high compared to online import stuff, sure, but what they carry is name-brand and the markup isn't unreasonable if you can get something now instead of waiting for shipping.<//Review>

<username>Curtis Woo</username>< pics>
None</pics>
<Text>I was referred here by my favorite hardware store, the Grand Lake Ace Hardware, so I had high expectations.  They were exceeded by the level of expertise, friendliness, inventory and pricing that I experienced, and continue to experience, at this local wonderland of electronics.  This is a family owned business and has been around for decades.  To the easily intimidated or those looking for a pack of AA batteries, don't be overwhelmed by the dizzying array of items that greets you upon opening the door.  Rest easy that the smiling faces behind the counter can and will answer any question you might have.  I am a long time DIY tinkerer and can well appreciate the vastness and power of the Internet.  From eBay to Parts Exress to Deals Extreme, I know I can usually find any electronic part on the web.  However, when I don't know what I'm looking for, but I do know the application I am planning, the web can be a cold and lonely place with only the sometime dubious advice of the user forums and discussion boards to give suggestions.  This is where Al Lasher's comes to the rescue nearly every time.  They have provided many a solution to the kinds of hurdles that every DIY tinkerer comes across mid-build of an electronics project.  Whether is is that perfect DPDT toggle I needed, the 12v SAE bullet connector, or that single 4000uf mylar capacitor that had the cell phone salesperson at Radio Shack busy Googling to see what it looked like (true story), the Lashers have come through.  They know exactly which row of which stack of what shelf to locate any part and, unlike most places these days, you can buy a single part rather than a 12-pack.  Seriously, when I needed to replace an led in my car's dashboard that the dealer wanted to charge $400 for and Amazon's vendor was selling by the dozens only, a visit to Al Lasher's netted me just the part I needed.  $.75 later the dash was back to its backlit glory.  Check them out, there's no other place I know of like it in the bay area (if anyone says "what about Fry's Electronics" smack them in the face).< /Text></record></dataset><record>
